<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Umbrella (song)</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<p>"<b>Umbrella</b>" is a song by Barbadian singer <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a> from her third studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Girl_Gone_Bad" title="Good Girl Gone Bad">Good Girl Gone Bad</a></i> (2007). It features American rapper <a href="/wiki/Jay_Z" title="Jay Z">Jay Z</a>, who co-wrote the song with its producers <a href="/wiki/Tricky_Stewart" title="Tricky Stewart">Tricky Stewart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuk_Harrell" title="Kuk Harrell">Kuk Harrell</a>, with additional writing from <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>. The song was originally written with <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> in mind, but her label rejected it. "Umbrella" is a <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> song with <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip-hop</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_n%27_roll" title="Rock n' roll">rock</a> touches referring to a romantic and platonic relationship and the strength of that relationship.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> ranked the song number one on the 10 Best Singles of 2007, while <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> listed the song at number three on the 100 Best Songs of 2007. The song has earned Rihanna several awards and nominations. In 2007, the song won two awards at the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2007 MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, when it was nominated for four. At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_Grammy_Awards" title="2008 Grammy Awards">2008 Grammy Awards</a>, "Umbrella" also earned Rihanna and Jay Z a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap/Sung_Collaboration" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap/Sung Collaboration">Grammy Award for Best Rap/Sung Collaboration</a> in addition to receiving nominations for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Song_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Song of the Year">Song of the Year</a>. The song is also listed on <i>Rolling Stone</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_500_Greatest_Songs_of_All_Time" title="Rolling Stone's 500 Greatest Songs of All Time">The 500 Greatest Songs of All Time</a></i> at 412.</p>
<p>The song serves as the <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> to the album, and was released worldwide on March 29, 2007 through <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a>. "Umbrella" was a commercial success, topping the charts in Australia, Canada, Germany, Spain, the Republic of Ireland, Sweden, Switzerland, the United Kingdom, and the United States. In the United Kingdom, where the song's chart performance generated controversy<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> when the country was experiencing <a href="/wiki/2007_United_Kingdom_floods" title="2007 United Kingdom floods">excessive flooding and large amounts of rain</a> at the time, it was one of the most played songs on <a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">radio</a> in the 2000s (decade). It managed to stay at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> for 10 consecutive weeks, the longest run at number one for any single of that decade, and is also one of the few songs to top the chart for at least 10 weeks. The single was one of the highest digital debuts in the United States and remained at the top of the US <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">Billboard</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Hot 100</a> for seven consecutive weeks.</p>
<p>The single's accompanying music video was directed by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Applebaum" title="Chris Applebaum">Chris Applebaum</a> and features, among all, Rihanna's nude body covered in silver paint. The video earned Rihanna a <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Video_of_the_Year" title="MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year">Video of the Year</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2007 MTV Video Music Awards">2007 MTV Video Music Awards</a> and Most Watched Video on MuchMusic.com at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MuchMusic_Video_Awards" title="MuchMusic Video Awards">MuchMusic Video Awards</a>. Along with countless amateurs, "Umbrella" has been covered by several notable performers from a variety of musical genres, including <a href="/wiki/All_Time_Low" title="All Time Low">All Time Low</a>, the <a href="/wiki/The_Baseballs" title="The Baseballs">Baseballs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biffy_Clyro" title="Biffy Clyro">Biffy Clyro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manic_Street_Preachers" title="Manic Street Preachers">Manic Street Preachers</a>, <a href="/wiki/McFly" title="McFly">McFly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Shinoda" title="Mike Shinoda">Mike Shinoda</a> of <a href="/wiki/Linkin_Park" title="Linkin Park">Linkin Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/OneRepublic" title="OneRepublic">OneRepublic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vanilla_Sky_(band)" title="Vanilla Sky (band)">Vanilla Sky</a>. Rihanna performed the song at the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2007 MTV Movie Awards">2007 MTV Movie Awards</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_BRIT_Awards" title="2008 BRIT Awards">2008 BRIT Awards</a> and was the closing song of the "<a href="/wiki/Good_Girl_Gone_Bad_Tour" title="Good Girl Gone Bad Tour">Good Girl Gone Bad Tour</a>" (2008), the "<a href="/wiki/Last_Girl_on_Earth" title="Last Girl on Earth">Last Girl on Earth</a>" (2010), and the "<a href="/wiki/Loud_Tour" title="Loud Tour">Loud Tour</a>" (2011). It was included in the "<a href="/wiki/Diamonds_World_Tour" title="Diamonds World Tour">Diamonds World Tour</a>" (2013), and the "<a href="/wiki/Anti_World_Tour" title="Anti World Tour">Anti World Tour</a>" (2016).</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>American songwriter and producer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_Stewart_(music_producer)" title="Christopher Stewart (music producer)">Christopher "Tricky" Stewart</a> convened with <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">Terius "The-Dream" Nash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuk_Harrell" title="Kuk Harrell">Kuk Harrell</a> in January 2007 at the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>-based Triangle Studios to create new material. In the studio, Stewart was "messing around with a walloping <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hi-hat_(instrument)" title="Hi-hat (instrument)">hi-hat</a> sound", which he found in the free music software <a href="/wiki/GarageBand" title="GarageBand">GarageBand</a>, which is included in all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mac_computer" title="Mac computer">Mac computers</a>. With his attention caught by the sound, Nash asked Stewart what he was doing: "Oh, my Gosh, what is that beat?". When Stewart incorporated <a href="/wiki/Chord_(music)" title="Chord (music)">chords</a> onto the hi-hat, "immediately the word popped into [Nash's] head"; he went to the vocal booth and started singing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RosenPoll_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-RosenPoll-1">[1]</a></sup> Nash wrote the first two verses and the chorus over Stewart's skeleton track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> They quickly wrote the lyrics, completing the first verse in 60 seconds. They continued into writing, adding the <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a> while "[Stewart] would put the next chord". In a matter of hours, they had recorded a <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demo</a> of the track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RosenPoll_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-RosenPoll-1">[1]</a></sup> The song was written with American pop singer <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> in mind, whom Stewart had previously worked with on her 2003 single "<a href="/wiki/Me_Against_the_Music" title="Me Against the Music">Me Against the Music</a>". Stewart and Nash thought that Spears, who had "her personal life ... a little out of control" at the time, needed a hit as musical comeback.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RosenPoll_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-RosenPoll-1">[1]</a></sup> Spears was working on her fifth album, <i><a href="/wiki/Blackout_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Blackout (Britney Spears album)">Blackout</a></i>, so they sent a copy of the demo to Spears' management. However, Spears did not hear of the song because her label rejected it, claiming they had enough songs for her to record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the management's rejection of the track, Stewart and Nash dealt it out to other record labels. It was also given to English singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Taio_Cruz" title="Taio Cruz">Taio Cruz</a>, who failed to convince his record company to release it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> It was then opted by <a href="/wiki/The_Island_Def_Jam_Music_Group" title="The Island Def Jam Music Group">Island Def Jam</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">Antonio "L.A." Reid</a>, a friend of Stewart who established his first studio. By early February 2007, the demo was sent to Reid's right-hand woman, <a href="/wiki/Artists_and_repertoire" title="Artists and repertoire">A&amp;R</a> executive Karen Kwak, who passed it along to Reid with a message confirming that they had found a song suited for Rihanna, who was working on her third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Girl_Gone_Bad" title="Good Girl Gone Bad">Good Girl Gone Bad</a></i>, at the time. Reid immediately sent the demo to Rihanna, who was also positive of it: "When the demo first started playing, I was like, This is interesting, this is weird. ... But the song kept getting better. I listened to it over and over. I said, 'I need this record. I want to record it tomorrow."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RosenPoll_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-RosenPoll-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>When [Rihanna] recorded the 'ellas,' you knew it was about to be the jump-off and your life was about to change if you had anything to do with that record.</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_Stewart_(music_producer)" title="Christopher Stewart (music producer)">Tricky Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-3">[3]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>However, since it was the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a> season of 2007, Stewart and Nash eyed American R&amp;B singer <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a> for the demo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-3">[3]</a></sup> Upon calling them to set the record aside for Rihanna, Stewart had played it to an associate of Blige, subsequently promising the song to her. Having heard the move of the writers, Kwak began calling Stewart and his manager, Mark Stewart, incessantly. Meanwhile, considering Blige's nominations at the Grammys, Stewart and Nash agreed to wait for her response. However, Blige failed to hear the song in full due to her obligations to the Grammys at the time and "had to sign off on the record before her reps could accept it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Finally, Reid "stepped in, trading on his power-broker status and longstanding relationship with Stewart", and admits, "I made the producers an offer they couldn't refuse."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RosenPoll_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-RosenPoll-1">[1]</a></sup> By the time Reid had successfully persuaded Stewart's camp, they "just couldn't say no".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-3">[3]</a></sup> On giving up the record to Reid's camp, Mark Stewart comments, "We knew Rihanna's album would be out in a few months. Mary wasn't even in an album cycle yet. We made the sensible business decision."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RosenPoll_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-RosenPoll-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rihanna recorded the song, with vocal production by <a href="/wiki/Kuk_Harrell" title="Kuk Harrell">Thaddis "Kuk" Harrell</a>, in a <a href="/wiki/Westlake_Recording_Studios" title="Westlake Recording Studios">Westlake Recording Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>. Initially, Stewart admitted he was still reluctant as to whether Rihanna was the right artist to record the song, but following the recording of the "ella, ella" <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catch_phrase" title="Catch phrase">catch phrase</a>, he felt they were onto "something".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-3">[3]</a></sup> Following Rihanna's recording, Def Jam CEO-rapper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> added his <a href="/wiki/Rapping" title="Rapping">rap</a>. However, Jay-Z rewrote his verse without the awareness of Stewart and Nash. Stewart could not understand it, but later realized it made "sense" instead of the first version. Stewart noted that "from a songwriter's standpoint, he just really made it more about the song, with the metaphors about umbrellas and about the weather versus what he had before".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Umbrella" was released worldwide on March 29, 2007, debuting on Rihanna's Def Jam website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DefJam_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-DefJam-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The song was released digitally in the United Kingdom on May 14, 2007, along with its physical release following two weeks later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"Umbrella" is a <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> song with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hip-hop_music" title="Hip-hop music">rap</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_n%27_Roll" title="Rock n' Roll">rock</a> influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The song's musicscape is based on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hi-hat_(instrument)" title="Hi-hat (instrument)">hi-hat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesizers</a>, and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audio_distortion" title="Audio distortion">distorted</a> <a href="/wiki/Bassline" title="Bassline">bassline</a>. According to <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> magazine, the song's beat can be recreated through a drum loop from the <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> music-software program <a href="/wiki/GarageBand" title="GarageBand">GarageBand</a> (Vintage Funk Kit 03).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWBest07_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-EWBest07-14">[14]</a></sup> The song is written in the key of <a href="/wiki/B-flat_minor" title="B-flat minor">B <span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;">♭</span> minor</a>. The song's lyrics are written in the traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Verse-chorus_form" title="Verse-chorus form">verse-chorus form</a>. They open with a rap verse, and the hook "ella, ella" follows every chorus. A <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(music)" title="Bridge (music)">bridge</a> follows the second hook, and the song ends in a <a href="/wiki/Fade_(audio_engineering)" title="Fade (audio engineering)">fadeout</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Andy Kellman of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> commented: "'Umbrella' is [Rihanna's best song] to date, delivering mammoth if spacious drums, a towering backdrop during the chorus, and vocals that are somehow totally convincing without sounding all that impassioned - an ideal spot between trying too hard and boredom, like she might've been on her 20th take."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Alex Macpherson of British newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, "Umbrella" is "evidence" that Rihanna's "strict work ethic is paying off", adding that she "delivers [in the song] an impassioned declaration of us-against-the-world devotion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Tom Breihan of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a>, though he complimented the production, dismissed Rihanna's voice which "takes on an unpleasant icepick edge when she tries to fill the space between the slow-tempo beats", adding that the song is "uncompelling as event-pop, particularly because of the disconnect between Rihanna's cold, clinical delivery and the comforting warmth of the lyrics".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sal Cinquemani from <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slant_(magazine)" title="Slant (magazine)">Slant Magazine</a></i> wrote "That the song is just plain good, regardless of genre, proves that Jay and Rihanna, who's already scored hits across several formats with a string of singles that couldn't be more different from each other, are dedicated to producing quality hits—however frivolous they may be."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Quentin B. Huff of <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters.com</a> said that ""Umbrella" is a monster, so much so that I'll even confess to spending a portion of a rainy afternoon practicing the hook."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Jonah Weiner of <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> magazine called the song the album's highlight and stated that it "would be far less engrossing if it wasn't for the way Rihanna disassembles its ungainly title into 11 hypnotic, tongue-flicking syllables".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> Kelefa Sanneh described the song as "a space-age hip-pop song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The song has earned Rihanna several awards and nominations. In 2008, "Umbrella" earned Rihanna and Jay-Z a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/50th_Grammy_Awards" title="50th Grammy Awards">Grammy Award</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap/Sung_Collaboration" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap/Sung Collaboration">Best Rap/Sung Collaboration</a> in addition to receiving nominations for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Song_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Song of the Year">Song of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> "Umbrella" has also been recognized in various forms of accolades by the music press. The song is listed number three on the 100 Best Songs of 2007, published by the music magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine also listed the song number three on their Top 10 Songs of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> "Umbrella" is listed at number two on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/Pazz_%26_Jop" title="Pazz &amp; Jop">Pazz &amp; Jop</a> annual year-end critics' poll, behind <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse" title="Amy Winehouse">Amy Winehouse</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Rehab_(Amy_Winehouse_song)" title="Rehab (Amy Winehouse song)">Rehab</a>". The song is listed number one on <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> magazine's list of the 10 Best Singles of 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWBest07_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-EWBest07-14">[14]</a></sup> while topping the magazine's poll for the best single of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> <i>Blender</i> magazine awarded the song Song of the Year in their Readers' Poll 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RosenPoll_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-RosenPoll-1">[1]</a></sup> The music press has considered "Umbrella" as 2007's Song of the Summer,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> writer <a href="/wiki/Kelefa_Sanneh" title="Kelefa Sanneh">Kelefa Sanneh</a> regarded it as "arguably 2007's signature slow jam".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In 2009, Pitchfork ranked the song as the #25 song on list of The Top 500 Tracks of the decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> put it on its end-of-the-decade, "best-of" list, saying, "In 2007, Rihanna had us all singin' in the rain."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> On <i>Rolling Stone'</i>s updated version of their <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_500_Greatest_Songs_of_All_Time" title="The 500 Greatest Songs of All Time">The 500 Greatest Songs of All Time</a></i>, "Umbrella" was listed at number 412, making Rihanna one of the youngest living artists in that list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In October 2011, <i>NME</i> placed it at number 63 on its list "150 Best Tracks of the Past 15 Years".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chart_performance">Chart performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Chart performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"Umbrella" entered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Singles_Chart" title="Australian Singles Chart">Australian Singles Chart</a> at number one on June 10, 2007, becoming Rihanna's second number one in the country following "<a href="/wiki/SOS_(Rihanna_song)" title="SOS (Rihanna song)">SOS</a>" (2006). It spent six consecutive weeks at the top,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AustraliaChart_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-AustraliaChart-41">[41]</a></sup> and has since earned earned a 5× Platinum certification by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a>, denoting sales of 350,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AustraliaRihannaUmbrellasingleCertRef_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-AustraliaRihannaUmbrellasingleCertRef-42">[42]</a></sup> It spent a total of 32 weeks on the chart,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AustraliaChart_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-AustraliaChart-41">[41]</a></sup> ending the year as the country's third best-selling single of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> "Umbrella" debuted on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Singles_Chart" title="New Zealand Singles Chart">New Zealand Singles Chart</a> at number 34 on May 14, 2007. Over the following two weeks, it dropped one place, then climbed to a new peak of number 33. In its fourth week on the chart, it leaped to the top of the chart, becoming Rihanna's second number one single following "<a href="/wiki/Pon_de_Replay" title="Pon de Replay">Pon de Replay</a>" (2005).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewZealandChart_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-NewZealandChart-44">[44]</a></sup> It remained atop the chart for six consecutive weeks and on the chart for a total of 24 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewZealandChart_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-NewZealandChart-44">[44]</a></sup> The song received a Platinum certification from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_New_Zealand" title="Recording Industry Association of New Zealand">Recording Industry Association of New Zealand</a>, denoting sales of 15,000 copies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> subsequently becoming the country's best-selling single of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_Umbrella_Last_Girl_On_Earth_Tour_Zurich.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Rihanna_Umbrella_Last_Girl_On_Earth_Tour_Zurich.JPG/170px-Rihanna_Umbrella_Last_Girl_On_Earth_Tour_Zurich.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Rihanna_Umbrella_Last_Girl_On_Earth_Tour_Zurich.JPG/255px-Rihanna_Umbrella_Last_Girl_On_Earth_Tour_Zurich.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Rihanna_Umbrella_Last_Girl_On_Earth_Tour_Zurich.JPG/340px-Rihanna_Umbrella_Last_Girl_On_Earth_Tour_Zurich.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_Umbrella_Last_Girl_On_Earth_Tour_Zurich.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rihanna performing "Umbrella" in Zurich at her tour <a href="/wiki/Last_Girl_on_Earth" title="Last Girl on Earth">Last Girl on Earth</a>, 2010.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"Umbrella" debuted on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> on the chart issue dated April 28, 2007, at number 91.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_5_May_2007_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_5_May_2007-47">[47]</a></sup> The following week it climbed to number 72,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_5_May_2007_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_5_May_2007-47">[47]</a></sup> and to number 63 in its third week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In its fourth, fifth and sixth week on the chart, it progressively ascended to numbers 52,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_19_May_2007_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_19_May_2007-49">[49]</a></sup> 44<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_26_May_2007_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_26_May_2007-50">[50]</a></sup> and 41.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007-51">[51]</a></sup> Prior to its physical release, "Umbrella" achieved the biggest debut in the six-year history of <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> in the United States, breaking a record previously held by <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wyclef_Jean" title="Wyclef Jean">Wyclef Jean</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Hips_Don%27t_Lie" title="Hips Don't Lie">Hips Don't Lie</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez-3">[3]</a></sup> Following its digital release, "Umbrella" soared to number one for the issue dated June 9, 2007 on its seventh week on the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CohenRocket_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-CohenRocket-52">[52]</a></sup> It subsequently debuted atop the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Digital_Songs" title="Hot Digital Songs">Hot Digital Songs</a> chart, with first-week sales of over 277,000 units. The single became the highest digital debut in the United States since <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> began tracking downloads in 2003, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/SexyBack" title="SexyBack">SexyBack</a>" 250,000 sales record in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007-51">[51]</a></sup> The single's rise to the top of the Hot 100 marked Rihanna's second number one single following "<a href="/wiki/SOS_(Rihanna_song)" title="SOS (Rihanna song)">SOS</a>" (2006),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CohenRocket_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-CohenRocket-52">[52]</a></sup> which was also noted for its huge leap on the Hot 100 to the top spot based on digital sales alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Significantly sustained by the strong airplay of the single<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> and preventing American rap group <a href="/wiki/Shop_Boyz" title="Shop Boyz">Shop Boyz</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Party_Like_a_Rockstar" title="Party Like a Rockstar">Party Like a Rockstar</a>" from advancing on the chart, "Umbrella" spent seven consecutive weeks at the top of the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> "Umbrella" eventually became the second best-performing single of 2007 on the Hot 100, only behind <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>'s hit single "<a href="/wiki/Irreplaceable" title="Irreplaceable">Irreplaceable</a>" which topped the chart for ten weeks total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Umbrella" entered the top fifty of the US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_Songs" title="Radio Songs">Radio Songs</a> chart on the issue dated April 28, 2007, at number 42.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RadioDebut_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-RadioDebut-58">[58]</a></sup> The following week it climbed to number 29,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_5_May_2007_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_5_May_2007-47">[47]</a></sup> and reached the top twenty in its fourth week on the chart, at number 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_19_May_2007_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_19_May_2007-49">[49]</a></sup> It entered the top five of the chart on the chart issue of June 2, 2007, at number three.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_26_May_2007_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_26_May_2007-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007-51">[51]</a></sup> It eventually reached number one on the issue dated July 14, 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_14_Jul_2007_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_14_Jul_2007-59">[59]</a></sup> and remained at the top for four consecutive weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> On the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pop_Songs" title="Pop Songs">Pop Songs</a> chart, "Umbrella" debuted at number 77 on the chart issue dated April 28, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RadioDebut_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-RadioDebut-58">[58]</a></sup> The following week it rose to number 61,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RadioDebut_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-RadioDebut-58">[58]</a></sup> and to 51 in its third week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_5_May_2007_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_5_May_2007-47">[47]</a></sup> In its fourth week on the chart, it climbed to number 36.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> On the chart issue of June 9, 2007, "Umbrella" soared from number 31 to number one in its eighth week on the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007_51-3"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007-51">[51]</a></sup> It spent six consecutive weeks at the top.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_14_Jul_2007_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_14_Jul_2007-59">[59]</a></sup> "Umbrella" debuted at number 69 on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip_Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B/Hip Hop Songs</a> chart on the issue dated April 21, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The following week it rose to number 52<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RadioDebut_58-3"><a href="#cite_note-RadioDebut-58">[58]</a></sup> and by the issue dated June 9, 2007, it had climbed into the top twenty at number 17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007_51-4"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007-51">[51]</a></sup> It reached the top ten for the chart issue of June 16, 2007, and rose to number six the following week, earning the 'Greatest Gainer' in both sales and airplay for the week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_23_Jun_2007_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_23_Jun_2007-63">[63]</a></sup> It made its peak of number four in the issue of July 14, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_14_Jul_2007_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_14_Jul_2007-59">[59]</a></sup> "Umbrella" entered the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Songs" title="Hot Dance Club Songs">Hot Dance Club Songs</a> chart as the 'Hot Shot Debut' at number 36, for the issue dated June 9, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007_51-5"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_9_Jun_2007-51">[51]</a></sup> The following week it leaped to number 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> It ascended into the top ten of the chart the week after, landing at number nine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_23_Jun_2007_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_23_Jun_2007-63">[63]</a></sup> and rose to number four in its fourth week on the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> It topped the chart on the issue dated July 7, 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and remained at number one for a second week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_Magazine_-_14_Jul_2007_59-3"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_Magazine_-_14_Jul_2007-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of June 2015, "Umbrella" has sold 4,470,000 digital copies in the United States, and is Rihanna's sixth best-selling single in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_Sales_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_Sales-67">[67]</a></sup> The song debuted at number one in Canada, becoming the first song to top the then recently launched <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a>, a singles chart in Canada issued by <i>Billboard</i> magazine, similar to that of the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The single experienced major success, most notably, in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The song entered the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> at number one based on digital sales alone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> becoming Rihanna's first chart-topper in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> During the single's fourth week on the chart, Rihanna earned her first 'Chart Double' with both the single and subsequent album (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_Girl_Gone_Bad_(Rihanna_album)" title="Good Girl Gone Bad (Rihanna album)">Good Girl Gone Bad</a></i>) topping the UK Singles and <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">Albums</a> charts simultaneously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Having reached nine straight weeks at number one on the chart, it broke the record of American group <a href="/wiki/Gnarls_Barkley" title="Gnarls Barkley">Gnarls Barkley</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_(Gnarls_Barkley_song)" title="Crazy (Gnarls Barkley song)">Crazy</a>" as the longest chart-topper of the decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> "Umbrella" eventually reached a total of ten weeks at number one on the chart, becoming the country's longest-running number one single of the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> In addition, Rihanna become the seventh artist in history to top the chart for ten consecutive weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> By the end of 2008, "Umbrella" had sold over 600,000 copies, making it her biggest-selling single at the time, before being succeeded by "<a href="/wiki/Love_the_Way_You_Lie" title="Love the Way You Lie">Love the Way You Lie</a>", a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> two years later in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-official_charts_end_of_2010_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-official_charts_end_of_2010-76">[76]</a></sup> It became Britain's second biggest-selling single of 2007, only behind <a href="/wiki/Leona_Lewis" title="Leona Lewis">Leona Lewis</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Bleeding_Love" title="Bleeding Love">Bleeding Love</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> On December 12, 2008, it was certified Platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a>, for sales of 600,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-United_KingdomRihannaUmbrellasingleCertRef_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-United_KingdomRihannaUmbrellasingleCertRef-78">[78]</a></sup> In total, "Umbrella" has amassed 51 weeks in the official Charts, making it the joint 20th longest runner of all time. It has spent a further 20 weeks to tally 71 total weeks inside the Top 100, in which it has appeared in three consecutive years; number one in 2007, 18 in 2008 and number 99 in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Umbrella" had similar success elsewhere in Europe, topping charts for lengthy periods including Switzerland for nine weeks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Norway for seven weeks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Germany for five weeks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Austria for four weeks<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> and Belgium for three weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> It also reached number one in Denmark<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> and Hungary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In Spain, the song achieved an eight-times platinum certification from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PROMUSICAE" title="PROMUSICAE">PROMUSICAE</a>, denoting sales of over 160,000 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PROMUSICAE_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-PROMUSICAE-87">[87]</a></sup> Furthermore, "Umbrella" attained top five positions in the Czech Republic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IFPI_Czech_Republic_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-IFPI_Czech_Republic-88">[88]</a></sup> Finland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Italy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> the Netherlands<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> and Sweden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> It also reached the top ten of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Worldwide the song has sold more than 8.0 million copies, making it one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles" title="List of best-selling singles">best selling singles</a> of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ifpi2007_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-ifpi2007-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_video">Music video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Music video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_and_concept">Background and concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Background and concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While working on the album, ideas began to circulate concerning Rihanna's image, extending into her music videos. She asked American music video director <a href="/wiki/Chris_Applebaum" title="Chris Applebaum">Chris Applebaum</a> to send her "something" to work on. Def Jam representatives were expecting Applebaum of the treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez2_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez2-95">[95]</a></sup> In response, Applebaum hurriedly made a <a href="/wiki/Film_treatment" title="Film treatment">treatment</a> for the video, one of his first ideas being the silver body paint that Rihanna is seen in. Applebaum was doubtful whether Rihanna would embrace the idea, but her "positive response" following a letter the director sent to the artist ensured its approval. Makeup artist Pamela Neal mixed a silver paint that would give Rihanna such a look. During the session, the paint was re-applied between takes to ensure she was completely covered. The set was closed to Rihanna, Applebaum and a camera assistant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez2_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez2-95">[95]</a></sup> Rihanna also contributed her own ideas towards the video shoot, suggesting to Applebaum that she dance <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/En_pointe" title="En pointe">en pointe</a>, an idea which he accepted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rodriguez2_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rodriguez2-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>Visual effects at Kroma were supervised by Bert Yukich and produced by Amy Yukich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KromaInterview_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-KromaInterview-96">[96]</a></sup> A key part of the video is a 24-second visual effects sequence in which Rihanna is surrounded by silvery strands of liquid that crisscross the frame in graceful arcs in response to her movements. Water elements were recorded on a special effects stage using a high-speed 35mm camera. Bert Yukich then composited them into the scene with the singer. He then added lighting effects to the practical water elements to give them the mirror-like texture of mercury.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The music video premiered on April 26, 2007 at <a class="external text" href="http://www.islanddefjam.com/artist/home.aspx?artistID=7366" rel="nofollow">her website</a>. Downloads were made available for those in the U.S. only from the website for a limited time. The video was officially released on the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a> on May 11, 2007, peaking at number one for a period of eight weeks. On May 1, 2007, "Umbrella" debuted on MTV's <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">Total Request Live</a></i> at number 10, before reaching number one on May 9 where it remained for fifteen days, making it the longest running number one of 2007. The video was well-played in MTV during the second half of 2007; it has reached over 8,000 plays, receiving a platinum recognition at the MTV Platinum and Gold Video Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Such was the success of the promotional video that it received five nominations at the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2007 MTV Video Music Awards">2007 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, including "Female Artist of the Year", "Video of the Year" and "Monster Single of the Year", going on to win the latter two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id=".22Rihanna_Curse.22">"Rihanna Curse"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title='Edit section: "Rihanna Curse"'>edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Umbrella's reign at number one in the United Kingdom occurred as the country was hit by <a href="/wiki/2007_United_Kingdom_floods" title="2007 United Kingdom floods">extreme rainfall and flooding</a>, which led the British national newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> to humorously suggest the two events were related, with the media referring to it as the "Rihanna Curse." The tabloid also highlighted the date of the single's video shot which was <a href="/wiki/Friday_the_13th" title="Friday the 13th">Friday the 13th</a> (April 13, 2007), adding further coincidence of the curse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WostearCurse_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-WostearCurse-99">[99]</a></sup> Before the single's release on May 14, the temperature in London was relatively high, reaching 20 <a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">°C</a>. However, just a day after the release, "severe weather warnings hit the headlines".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WostearCurse_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-WostearCurse-99">[99]</a></sup> An article in <i>The Sun</i> urged readers to join the campaign to knock the song off the chart's top spot, suggesting to readers several other songs to download instead, all of which shared the theme of sunshine or summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WostearCurse_99-2"><a href="#cite_note-WostearCurse-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>A similar situation occurred in New Zealand, where the song hit number one in the early winter of 2007 as the country was experiencing some of the worst storms in its history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NZCurse_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-NZCurse-100">[100]</a></sup> During the weather conditions, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taranaki_Region" title="Taranaki Region">Taranaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tauranga" title="Tauranga">Tauranga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> had experienced tornadoes and flooding in the <a href="/wiki/Far_North_District" title="Far North District">Far North</a> of the country. Once the single was replaced on the top spot, weather conditions throughout New Zealand pacified, although <a href="/wiki/Hawke%27s_Bay_Region" title="Hawke's Bay Region">Hawke's Bay</a> was still stormy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NZCurse_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-NZCurse-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>The same happened in <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> where "Umbrella" hit the stations in the nation during the summer. That summer was in its first half the hottest and driest period of time in Romania since 1946.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-romania_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-romania-101">[101]</a></sup> As the song reached the top ten and then its number-one peak, the country experienced the worst storms and most pouring rains in its history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> As the song was losing positions in the charts, the storm ended and the temperatures lowered step-by-step.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-romania_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-romania-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pop_culture_and_gaming">Pop culture and gaming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Pop culture and gaming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_Performing_Umbrella.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="456" data-file-width="480" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Rihanna_Performing_Umbrella.jpg/220px-Rihanna_Performing_Umbrella.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Rihanna_Performing_Umbrella.jpg/330px-Rihanna_Performing_Umbrella.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Rihanna_Performing_Umbrella.jpg/440px-Rihanna_Performing_Umbrella.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_Performing_Umbrella.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rihanna performing "Umbrella" during the <a href="/wiki/Loud_Tour" title="Loud Tour">Loud Tour</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the record-breaking success of the single and the reported coincidence with the weather, Def Jam's marketing team collaborated with British umbrella manufacturer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Totes%C2%BBISOTONER" title="Totes»ISOTONER">Totes</a>. The company produced five types of Rihanna umbrellas, one of which was a two-tone satin umbrella that Rihanna debuted in public during her performance of the song at the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2007 MTV Movie Awards">2007 MTV Movie Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Although manufactured by a UK-based company, the collection was made available only to US residents online through the company's website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Krystal Weedon, one of the central characters in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J.K._Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling">J.K. Rowling</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Casual_Vacancy" title="The Casual Vacancy">The Casual Vacancy</a></i>, was very apt at doing Jay-Z's rap from "Umbrella" during their rowing competition bus trips. "Umbrella", to the shock of the attendees, is also played at the church during the funeral service of Barry Fairbrother who used to coach the girls' rowing team prior to his death. Similarly, the song was also played at the funeral service of another character.</p>
<p>In November 2007 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MADtv" title="MADtv">MADtv</a>'s Nicole Parker and Keegan-Michael Key, who were impersonating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)_presidential_primaries,_2008" title="Democratic Party (United States) presidential primaries, 2008">U.S. Democratic presidential candidates</a> <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> respectively, performed a parody of "Umbrella".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Umbrella" has been featured in the <a href="/wiki/Karaoke" title="Karaoke">karaoke</a> <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a> <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_songs_in_SingStar_games_(PlayStation_2)" title="List of songs in SingStar games (PlayStation 2)">SingStar Pop Volume 2</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Lips_(video_game)" title="Lips (video game)">Lips</a></i>, both accompanied by the music video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGNreviewlips_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-IGNreviewlips-106">[106]</a></sup> A cover of the song is also featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Dance_Dance_Revolution_Hottest_Party_2" title="Dance Dance Revolution Hottest Party 2">Dance Dance Revolution Hottest Party 2</a></i> as a playable track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ddroc.hp2media_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-ddroc.hp2media-107">[107]</a></sup> The original version of the song appears in dance games <i><a href="/wiki/Just_Dance_4" title="Just Dance 4">Just Dance 4</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dance_Central_3" title="Dance Central 3">Dance Central 3</a></i> as DLC.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"Umbrella" was performed by Rihanna during the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2007 MTV Movie Awards">2007 MTV Movie Awards</a> on June 3, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, she performed the song on the ITV morning show <a href="/wiki/GMTV" title="GMTV">GMTV</a> and on <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">The Brit Awards</a> in 2008. She also performed "Umbrella" during her <a href="/wiki/AOL" title="AOL">AOL</a> sessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In France, she performed it on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_Academy_(France)" title="Star Academy (France)">Star Academy</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> "Umbrella" was added to the setlist of her first headlining <a href="/wiki/Good_Girl_Gone_Bad_Tour" title="Good Girl Gone Bad Tour">Good Girl Gone Bad Tour</a> where it was performed as the final song for the encore. It was also included as the closing act of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_Girl_on_Earth_Tour" title="Last Girl on Earth Tour">Last Girl on Earth Tour</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Loud_Tour" title="The Loud Tour">The Loud Tour</a>. Rihanna performed "Umbrella" at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_1%27s_Big_Weekend#2012" title="Radio 1's Big Weekend">Radio 1's Hackney Weekend</a> on May 24, 2012, as the sixteenth song on the set list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hackney_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hackney-111">[111]</a></sup> The performance featured a giant <a href="/wiki/Sphinx" title="Sphinx">sphinx</a> on the stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> The song is also performed during the <a href="/wiki/Diamonds_World_Tour" title="Diamonds World Tour">Diamonds World Tour</a> and the 'Anti World Tour'.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_versions_and_remixes">Cover versions and remixes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Cover versions and remixes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DJ_Earworm_NYE_Singapore_2009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="638" data-file-width="960" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/DJ_Earworm_NYE_Singapore_2009.jpg/220px-DJ_Earworm_NYE_Singapore_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/DJ_Earworm_NYE_Singapore_2009.jpg/330px-DJ_Earworm_NYE_Singapore_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/DJ_Earworm_NYE_Singapore_2009.jpg/440px-DJ_Earworm_NYE_Singapore_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DJ_Earworm_NYE_Singapore_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/DJ_Earworm" title="DJ Earworm">DJ Earworm</a> used "Umbrella" as the base track for his breakthrough mash-up, "United State of Pop", which combined Billboard's Top 25 songs of 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Then-upcoming singer <a href="/wiki/Mari%C3%A9_Digby" title="Marié Digby">Marié Digby</a> recorded an acoustic version of "Umbrella" which was released August 3, 2007 as the debut single from her <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Records" title="Hollywood Records">Hollywood Records</a> <i>Start Here EP</i> and included as the closing track on Digby's debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Unfold_(Mari%C3%A9_Digby_album)" title="Unfold (Marié Digby album)">Unfold</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BuzzDigby_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-BuzzDigby-196">[196]</a></sup> Scottish rock group <a href="/wiki/Biffy_Clyro" title="Biffy Clyro">Biffy Clyro</a> also released an acoustic version of the song,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> just like the Italian singer <a href="/wiki/Neja_(singer)" title="Neja (singer)">Neja</a> has done in her cover – album <i>Acousticlub</i>, while <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a> band <a href="/wiki/Vanilla_Sky_(band)" title="Vanilla Sky (band)">Vanilla Sky</a> went in the opposite direction and released a punk cover of the song,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> and Norwegian band <a href="/wiki/Egil_Hegerberg" title="Egil Hegerberg">Bare Egil Band</a> have made a <a href="/wiki/Doom_metal" title="Doom metal">doom metal</a> version of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>For her debut album <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=A.K.a._Cassandra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="A.K.a. Cassandra (page does not exist)">a.K.a. Cassandra</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Filipina</a> singer and actress <a href="/wiki/KC_Concepcion" title="KC Concepcion">KC Concepcion</a> covered the song in English, while singer Miss Ganda recorded a version in <a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">Filipino</a> entitled "Payong" (which means umbrella in Filipino).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> Singer and actress <a href="/wiki/Mandy_Moore" title="Mandy Moore">Mandy Moore</a> sang an acoustic version of the song in 2007 and its video on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> has more than 5,700,000 views by November, 2012 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pop-punk outfit <a href="/wiki/All_Time_Low" title="All Time Low">All Time Low</a> covered the song for the <a href="/wiki/Fearless_Records" title="Fearless Records">Fearless Records</a> compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/Punk_Goes_Crunk" title="Punk Goes Crunk">Punk Goes Crunk</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> and British rock band <a href="/wiki/Manic_Street_Preachers" title="Manic Street Preachers">Manic Street Preachers</a> produced their own version of "Umbrella", which was originally recorded for the album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NME_Awards_2008_(album)" title="NME Awards 2008 (album)">NME Awards 2008</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> Produced in celebration of the <a href="/wiki/NME_Awards" title="NME Awards">Shockwaves NME Awards</a> 2008 and Big Gig, that album was given free with a special souvenir box set of the magazine <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> on February 27. Two additional versions (acoustic and Grand Slam mix) were later made available on iTunes, and the trio is now released together on an <i>Umbrella EP</i>; a video for the cover is available on the band's official website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<p>British <a href="/wiki/Pop_rock" title="Pop rock">pop rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/McFly" title="McFly">McFly</a> performed their own version of "Umbrella" during their Greatest Hits So Far Tour in 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finnish</a> <a href="/wiki/Melodic_death_metal" title="Melodic death metal">melodic death metal</a> band <a href="/wiki/Children_of_Bodom" title="Children of Bodom">Children of Bodom</a> performed their 2008 cover live at <a href="/wiki/Wacken_Open_Air" title="Wacken Open Air">Wacken Open Air</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> Country-pop singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a> recorded a live version of the song, which was later included in an <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a> exclusive <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> titled <i>Live from SoHo – EP</i> (2008).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Her version of the song peaked at number seventy-nine on <a href="/wiki/Pop_100" title="Pop 100"><i>Billboard</i> Pop 100</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<p>There have also been notable mixed versions of the song. American rapper <a href="/wiki/Lil_Mama" title="Lil Mama">Lil Mama</a> recorded a version of "Umbrella" that replaced Jay-Z's opening rap verse. An article by <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> magazine, who dismissed Jay-Z's version, said "Lil Mama actually seems to understand the song's metaphorical themes of protection and loyalty".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> American punk band <a href="/wiki/Blink-182" title="Blink-182">Blink-182</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Travis_Barker" title="Travis Barker">Travis Barker</a> remixed the song, adding to the track "quicksilver snare flourishes and... real-life guitars".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlenderRemix_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-BlenderRemix-210">[210]</a></sup></p>
<p>Singer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chris_Brown_(American_singer)" title="Chris Brown (American singer)">Chris Brown</a> created an <a href="/wiki/Answer_song" title="Answer song">answer song</a> titled "Cinderella", replacing some of the verses and part of the chorus of "Umbrella" with his own lyrics. This version is the official remix. This version has been performed as a duet between Brown and Rihanna when he joined Rihanna on a late-2008 tour in the Asia-Pacific region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> R&amp;B/hip-hop singer <a href="/wiki/The-Dream" title="The-Dream">The-Dream</a>, who wrote "Umbrella", recorded the <a href="/wiki/Demo_(music)" title="Demo (music)">demo</a> with a slightly different intro and instrumental.</p>
<p>Recently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2011)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup>, Korean girl group <a href="/wiki/2NE1" title="2NE1">2NE1</a> covered this song on Music Bank. The song's drum beat is sampled in "Symphonies" by <a href="/wiki/Dan_Black" title="Dan Black">Dan Black</a>. An episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i> featured this song performed by <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(music)" title="Mashup (music)">mash-up</a> with "<a href="/wiki/Singin%27_in_the_Rain_(song)" title="Singin' in the Rain (song)">Singin' in the Rain</a>". The song has also been covered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiffany_(Korean_singer)" title="Tiffany (Korean singer)">Tiffany</a>, an American-Korean singer from the popular girl group <a href="/wiki/Girls%27_Generation" title="Girls' Generation">Girls' Generation</a> in their first Asia Tour. In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> incorporated the "Eh, Eh" hook for her song "<a href="/wiki/Eh,_Eh_(Nothing_Else_I_Can_Say)" title="Eh, Eh (Nothing Else I Can Say)">Eh, Eh (Nothing Else I Can Say)</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washington_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-washington-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of 2007, Internet <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(music)" title="Mashup (music)">mash-up</a> artist <a href="/wiki/DJ_Earworm" title="DJ Earworm">DJ Earworm</a> used "Umbrella" as the base track for "United State of Pop", his breakthrough mix that included <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Year-End_Hot_100_singles_of_2007" title="Billboard Year-End Hot 100 singles of 2007">the top 25 songs on Billboard's Hot 100 year-end chart of 2007</a> (on which "Umbrella" appeared at #2).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> On Friday, August 28, 2015, country music duo Maddie and Tae covered it on the Bobby Bones Show.</p>
<p>On October 15, 2015, Scott Bradlee's <a href="/wiki/Postmodern_Jukebox" title="Postmodern Jukebox">Postmodern Jukebox</a> released a "Singin' in the Rain" style cover, featuring Casey Abrams &amp; The Sole Sisters, surpassing 1.8mil views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Baseballs_version">The Baseballs version</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umbrella_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: The Baseballs version">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>"Umbrella" was covered by the <a href="/wiki/Rockabilly" title="Rockabilly">rockabilly</a> coverband, <a href="/wiki/The_Baseballs" title="The Baseballs">The Baseballs</a>, in 2009. It was certified Platinum in Finland by <a href="/wiki/Musiikkituottajat_%E2%80%93_IFPI_Finland" title="Musiikkituottajat – IFPI Finland">Musiikkituottajat – IFPI Finland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup></p>
